ËŒÉ‘ m ËˆÉ‘ n d o l É‘ , >* , >* , >* , >* , >* , >* , m ËˆÉ› n d u lË  $almond. Feminine. Orel 1998: 256. AMYGDALA need not be the form cited -- the REW (number 436, p30) cotes attested amyndala as a headword as well as an *amandola, and -nd- or regularly reflected -nn- forms are seen in Sicilian, Tarentine, Neapolitan, Abruzzese, Logudorese, Portuguese, French (al(e)mande via metathesis > English almond); Romanian migdalÄƒ is from Greek per the REW. Going with the Romance form 3 from the REW (may consider adding the #2, amyndala).

d ËŒiË r ËˆeË k t u m , >* , >* , >* , d É™ É¾ ËˆÉ› j t , >* , >* , d É¾ ËˆÉ› j t $adj, direct, straight, right, just, correct. Orel 1998: 73; but Orel 1998(:17) also posits it as a lone from "Dalmatian (i.e. Western) Romance" along with trajteÌˆ and pajtoj. Bonnet 1998 has drejt and drejteÌˆ as separate etyma from the same source; Bonnet pp260, 348 on relation to deÌˆreq, ndreq, dreqteÌˆ -- deÌˆreq and drejteÌˆ attested in Buzuku, adverb dreq in Cham, Gjirokaster, Arbereshe, Arvanitika; Cabej 1958 (cited in Bonnet 1998: 260) attributes this to a local q/j alteration in the south. Treating the final -eÌˆ as orthographic here as it is not sounded in the standard and may function to signal the -a fpl form of the adjective. Comparison to Old Romanian derept -- Vatasescu 1997(:35), Cabej 1987: 312.

$now in ADoLex only; stress shift is accounted for regularly. d Ëˆu r r É‘ tÍ¡Êƒ u m , >* , >* , >* , >* , >* , >* , d Ëˆu r É™ s $DurreÌˆs. This is a NOVEL PROPOSAL though foreshadowed by Bonnet 1998(:37)'sa remarks about the outcome -s- from what looks like a Latin and Greek /kÊ°iu-/, rather than the expected /c/ <q>. Italian likewise has Durazzo rather than expected Duraccio; Slavic DracÌŒ. The idea here is that the Latin Durrachium and perhaps the Greek Dyrrhakhium actually overlie a Proto-Albanian /tÊƒ/ (using this sound as it is what is used in Proto-Albanian as the reflex of PIE *kÊ· before i/e by De Vaan 2018 and Orel 2000), rather than a /kiu/ or /kju/, which is plausible as this sound was lacking in both languages. Regarding the accent, once we no longer have the penultimate -I-, then the /u/ becomes antepenultimate, and the stress on it falls out easily from this proposal! f l ËˆÉ‘ k u l É‘ , >* , >* , >* , >* , >* , >* , f l Ëˆa k É™ $flame. Plural flakeÌˆra (Gheg flakeÌˆna). Cf Romanian flacÄƒrÄƒ, Italian fiaccola. Orel 1998: 98-9 as a "backformation" of a *flakull, itself from "dialectal" Romance flacula evinced in Romanian flacÄƒrÄƒ, Italian fiaccola, replacing facula "little torch". Note however Campidanese Sardinian flake (Meyer 1891: 107; Bonnet 1998: 271). This seems close to the view of Burr 1975(:63-4). Ã‡abej 1960 argued for a native Albanian formation based on the semantic richness, arguing for an elementary creation on an "expressive base". However, as Bonnet 1998(: 272), these semantic developments are all to parallel to those seen in Romance, especially in Romanian flacÄƒrÄƒ and Istriot fagla. Bonnet 1998(: 272, 379) defends the original etymology of facula here as either a Late Latin or Albanian-internal metathesis, the latter from a *fakÃ«l -- though in all of these cases, the plural in -Ã«ra (Gheg -Ã«na) would have had to be innovated pretty early. Admittedly this is a productive suffix (Orel 2000: 229). Proposal that the plural is actually the regularly reflected form, from a Romance flacula (per Burr 1975, Orel 1998 etc) embedded below.

É¡ Ëˆe n t e m , >* , >* , >* , >* , >* , >* , ÉŸ Ëˆi n d $folk, people. Per Orel 1998(: 136), plural only; masculine, as gjinde, may instead be from pl. gen. gentium -- or from some Italian variety later. Orel 2000(:27) argues it is a "later Latin" loan, but from Latin. However De Vaan 2017(:1743) and Bonnet 1998(:57, 143, 380) use gjind unproblematically from gentem, and gjind is also the citation form in Newmark 1998(: 285), not gjinde. Bonnet 1998(: 116) does observe regional differences however: gjeÌˆndeÌˆje in Southern Albania, gjind skewing toward Gheg (and lacking a nasal vowel), and gjende in Greece. Bonnet 1998(: 292) notes a "gjint". Matasovic 2024: 64 as gjinde.

$ËŒi n w ËŒe r n ËˆiË n u m , >* , >* , >* , v É™ r ËˆiÌƒË , >* , >* , v É™ r Ëˆi $winter pasture. Gheg: veÌˆrriÌ‚. Vs. hiberninum hypothesis. Generally attributed to hiberninumË Gheg: veÌˆrriÌ‚. $m ËŒÉ‘ n t ËˆiË l e , >* , >* , >* , >* , >* , >* , m a n d Ëˆi l É› $kerchief, per Orel 2000: 57. This one is difficult. Maybe Orel's right and it's regular, but it seems quite weird. Could also be a mantilia? Moved from Latin to Middle Greek into Late Proto-Albanian II.
